de emigraine	 Of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez Â«cultellareÂ» tant quâ€™il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et lâ€™estrain que tu ne coper lâ€™artere et que ne viegnes juscâ€™a lâ€™os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners nâ€™ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de lâ€™artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne sâ€™i conoit, et qui nâ€™est estudians et esprovez; et laisse lâ€™uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre. de la dolor des dens	 Of toothache

li cure dou trembler	 the treatment of the trembling

dou reume des eulz	 Of the king of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 When acute cataracts come to anyone and you see the eyes cloudy and small, and weakening the vision, and the eyelids are burning; and the hair falls out, and there is a headache with it, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those humors and that cataract do not come from one vein, but rather many. And the appropriate treatment for this is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And it is that you instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a great slit in the middle of the forehead, and another on either side of the temples.

And begin from the slit of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert cotton between the two lips of the slit, and place linen tents over it; then bandage with cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when they are removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with drying substances that promote flesh growth.

de lâ€™estoupement des oreilles	 of the bursting of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui nâ€™ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens lâ€™oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en lâ€™oreille, si câ€™on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 No child is born without any opening in the ears; and the same thing happens to adults when there is a bursting of a wound or growth of flesh within the ear, and this bursting sometimes goes deep into the ear so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is a lack of the opening, and one can see it well.

de la gresle	 of gravel

Exinach is a fat that is entangled in the tissues of the eyelids above, and this happens more to children than to any other people, and it greatly grieves their eyes, and catarrh comes to them in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they often lie on their faces, and sleep on them, and their eyelids beneath are moistened so that swelling and inflammation cover the exinach that appears in the eye.

des apostemes des levres	 of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprÃ©s lâ€™incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive dâ€™aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 In many men, hard abscesses like grains of millet occur within the lips, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut into each knot, and take it with the tweezers and chop it in every part; then fill the place after the incision with crushed vitriol until the blood is clotted; and then apply aloes and treat the place with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent Â«albulusÂ»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprÃ©s lâ€™incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprÃ©s le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Many times a fleshy growth appears on the gums, which the ancients called Â«albulusÂ»; then you must grasp it with tongs and cut it at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then apply to the spot ground vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: then it does not return after cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiÃ©s soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant quâ€™il nâ€™i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant quâ€™elles soient mondees; et sâ€™on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, câ€™est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes dâ€™estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Sometimes there are unsightly and rough scabs gathered at the root of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums; sometimes the teeth turn black and yellowish-green, until the corruption reaches the gum, making the teeth stink; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and hold his head in your lap, and scrape away the teeth or the scabs until nothing remains; and do the same with the blackness and greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are completely removed; and know that the teeth need different forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work shows, because the scrapers used to scrape outside the teeth have different shapes from those used to scrape between the teeth; and let these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car câ€™est une substance mout haute juscâ€™a donc câ€™on nâ€™ait point dâ€™excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary that when you cure the tooth of its pain, you delay pulling it as much as possible, for this should not be done at all; because it is a very noble substance up to the point where one has no excuse for pulling it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is forced to pull out the tooth, it is necessary that you are certain about the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide quâ€™elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos lâ€™avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant quâ€™il soit bien eslochiÃ©s, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiÃ©s dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si quâ€™il ne se mueve.	 Often the pain deceives the patient and thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and makes him pull out the good tooth; nevertheless, the pain does not depart from this, until the evil root is pulled out, for we have already seen this happen to these lords; and when you are certain about the aching tooth, it is necessary that you cauterize around the tooth in all directions; then move it with your fingers or fine tweezers bit by bit, until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the tweezers; and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
AprÃ©s estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et sâ€™il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it gently into each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu lâ€™emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si lâ€™estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a lâ€™estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is decayed and rotten, it must be filled with cloth where the holes are; and hold it delicately with the pliers so that it does not break while being held; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And beware well that you do not break it and a part remains, and the patient will suffer greater pain than before due to the rootâ€™s malice.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et nâ€™i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par lâ€™oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit quâ€™il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou dâ€™aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act like the ignorant practitioners who, through their haste and recklessness, sometimes break the bone, and do not bring what we have mentioned, but often cause great illness due to the roots left behind or the broken bone, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood flows from it, which often happens, fill the area with burnt vitriol; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, quâ€™il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens primer, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, quâ€™il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:
Et soient de gros membres si quâ€™il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And they should be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made iron, and they should have teeth to keep a firm hold.

quant li dent lochent	 When the teeth are dislocated
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu quâ€™il menjue quâ€™il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre dâ€™un fil dâ€™or, car li filz dâ€™argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de lâ€™espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiÃ©s entre les dens meus, sâ€™il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement juscâ€™au dent sain dâ€™autre part; puis rencomence la coverture juscâ€™a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant quâ€™il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si quâ€™il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth are dislocated, either by striking or falling, and the patient cannot bite onto what they are eating without them falling out, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, and that does not work; then they must be restrained with a golden thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the knots between the loose teeth, whether there is one or several, so that you wisely reach up to the other healthy tooth; then start the covering again from the point where you began, and delicately and wisely tighten your hand until it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiÃ©s dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi quâ€™il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et sâ€™il deslie, ou li filz ront, si lâ€™estraint dâ€™un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et câ€™est li forme des dens et li figure de lâ€™adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Puis cope les chiÃ©s dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, and put the heads of the wire together with pliers, and place them between the healthy tooth, and position it so that it does not injure the tongue; and then leave it as close as possible while it remains in place, and if it comes loose, or the wires break, then hold it with another wire; thus it will remain and serve throughout its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of two healthy teeth, and two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne sâ€™en entremette mie qui nâ€™est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme dâ€™un dent dâ€™os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et lâ€™estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, and when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, de fres en fres, freshly as we have said; et ne sâ€™en entremette mie qui nâ€™est saiges et soffrans, and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, et aucune fois fait on la forme dâ€™un dent dâ€™os de vaiche, and sometimes make the shape of a tooth from cow bone, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, and place it in the location where the defect is, et lâ€™estraint on si com nos avons dit, and hold it as we have said, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens. and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 of copper for the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et câ€™est de soudement de plaie, si i boute lâ€™uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por lâ€™artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu dâ€™aigue rose et dâ€™aisil, ou dâ€™aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes this ligament comes naturally from beneath the tongue at birth; or by accident due to a healed wound; and the operation is such that you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your lap, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, which comes from the sudden healing of a wound, then insert the hook and cut widely that ligament; and be careful that the split is not too deep for the artery that is beneath; and when you have done this, lift the area with rose water and aloes, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen bandage; and the patient should dress the area each night, so that it may not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure dâ€™autre cure tant quâ€™il soit sanez,	 Et si la perte de sang continue, applique une pommade Ã  base de vitriol sur la plaie ; et si le saignement persiste, cautÃ©rise avec un cautÃ¨re lentigineux, qui est bon pour cela ; puis traite d'une autre maniÃ¨re jusqu'Ã  ce qu'il soit guÃ©ri.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si nâ€™i touchier point, car câ€™est chancre; et sâ€™il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete lâ€™oncine, et lou fent dâ€™un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre dâ€™une part et dâ€™autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant quâ€™il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu dâ€™aisil et de seil, et le cure dâ€™autres cures tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if you see the flesh colored black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it inclines to be pustulous, and there is moisture, apply alum, and open it with a fine spatula, and deliver it from both sides; and if the bleeding persists during your work, place vitriol pomade on it until it becomes stained, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the pus; then lift the flesh with ease and silk, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 of the throat abscesses

Sometimes abscesses come into the throat which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and of dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et sâ€™il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant quâ€™il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et sâ€™il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet lâ€™estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for fear of bleeding; but let it remain until it becomes soft, and then you will divide it, or it would burst on its own; and if it turns pale again, and the root is delicate, have the instrument prepared to cut, but first check if the abscess is calm and soothed.

Et je medicinai une femme dâ€™un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, câ€™est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte sâ€™elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, to be precise, the abscess of little sense; and it had nearly closed off her entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez quâ€™il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced out two teeth through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en lâ€™un I oncine, puis lou traÃ¯ fuers, et en traÃ¯ grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en lâ€™autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprÃ©s fichai lâ€™oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et nâ€™en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adÃ©s, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant quâ€™il refut mout gros; adonques je lâ€™engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprÃ©s moi.	 I hurried therefore immediately and inserted a needle into one [nostril], then drew it out, and with it drained a large portion of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, and I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the needle into this abscess, and I drained some of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus was the passage of the woman's throat cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess would always grow back again, filling the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I packed it with cloth and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it ceased to grow; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me.
de lâ€™uve	 of the grape
Quant reume dessent a lâ€™uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee Â«perpendiculaireÂ»; et sâ€™elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee Â«uveÂ».	 When pus descends to the grape and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is low and round, it is called "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et nâ€™est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues lâ€™incision de li.	 When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the incision does not help, and you see that the underlying abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then you must remove it; and the one that is round and assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or the color of pitch or black, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que jâ€™ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a lâ€™estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche lâ€™oncine en lâ€™uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que jâ€™ai dit en lâ€™incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, of its color and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument as we have recalled before; then insert the onion into the grape, and draw it out from below, and cut it off at one-half to two-thirds of the length that I have said in the incision of the almond.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprÃ©s lâ€™incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en lâ€™incision des II amandres, et le cure tant quâ€™elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you cut no more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use dâ€™engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you should use ingenuity for the cautery to remove their fear.

de la sansue de la gorge	 of the blood from the throat

li chapistres des apostemes	 And the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances dâ€™aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprÃ©s dâ€™un et dâ€™autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et câ€™est en II manieres dont lâ€™une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu quâ€™il tient moistor.	 There are many types of abscesses, as will be remembered hereafter in this book and others, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and there are two kinds: one is like itself, and the other retains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second type is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en lâ€™uevre.	 car the abscess of the head is different from that of the fundament, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in joints, and each should be judged in its work.
Et si a apostemes câ€™on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz quâ€™il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is ripe according to its development; and there are those which one must pierce when they are hardened, and do not ripen according to their development, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant quâ€™il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when an abscess comes near the joints, and one lets it be until it is ripe all around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant quâ€™il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois quâ€™il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, quâ€™il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Where the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; where it is near the fundament, perforate it as soon as it is ripe; and one should not perforate an abscess before digestion is complete, except for those near the fundament, lest it putrefy deeper, become elongated inside, and a fistula develops; and it cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches lâ€™oure de la perforation de lâ€™aposteme qui est meur selonc lâ€™acomplissement, et câ€™est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et lâ€™amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de lâ€™aguisement dou chief de lâ€™aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de lâ€™aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il nâ€™a point de ploieure.	 And you should know the hour of perforation of the abscess that is ripe according to completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the separation of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and the weakening and softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be done in the most dependent place of the abscess, where it opens best; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no flexibility.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 En ceux qui sont penchÃ©s, selon cet membre.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant quâ€™il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout dâ€™ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, the body will be filled with poison from it, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is an abscess that has been pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs from it.

And you should make small holes in small abscesses, and large holes in large abscesses, and many slits according to the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cauterize with a spoon and cover; when they have become like rags and are dead, then you should do as one does with buboes: and there are such which are split into three angles, and there are such which are cut like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the anus; and there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar cauterizations.

Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce it thoroughly; and if the abscess is large and has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again; do this many times from great to small, until all the pus comes out; likewise if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.

Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have noticed your abscess, wash the wound, and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a plain incision, bring ten linen cloths or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must insert one tent into each so that they touch each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of leather, and you have taken it out whole, then you must fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 so it is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it and pulling strongly, and sew as we have said.

de squinance	 of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et câ€™est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke and talked about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee Â«epigloteÂ» soit eschuee; et câ€™on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the cleft of the throat called "epiglottis" be cut; and one does not help with this because all the veins and the lungs of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.

Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre lâ€™epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de lâ€™epiglote quâ€™il nâ€™i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc dâ€™enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it between III or IV small transverse circles, between II and III circles or according to the amount of the syphac fissure, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no bone there, and the vessels are long.

And if the master is afraid, he must extend the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cut through the heart until it reaches the esophagus; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut off the liver as we have said; and it is proven by the section of the phlegm of the esophagus which jumps strongly where it is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.

Albucasim dist câ€™on ne faice ce juscâ€™a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and there is a lack of air.
Adonques cope on lâ€™epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant quâ€™elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then they cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus he is saved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, which passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the cartilage of the larynx; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien quâ€™elle nâ€™avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I uncovered the wound and found that blood had escaped from it. Although neither a vein nor an artery was cut, a strong wind was blowing from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant quâ€™elle fut sanee; et nâ€™avint a la damoisele fuer quâ€™elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprÃ©s a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de lâ€™epiglote nâ€™ait mie paour.	 I hastened and sewed the wound, treating it until it was healed; nothing more happened to the maiden except that she lost her voice, which later returned to normal; therefore, I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 from the large throat

des nous	 of our
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many manners of us are, all of which I will speak of the likenesses; and now it is necessary that I say all the differences that are between our (thing) and issue (discharge).
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor. The same thing happens with an inflamed vein and abscess; and one recognizes this when it is due to the artery, for then the abscess is long and deep; and when you touch it with your fingers, you feel a constriction; and when it is due to the vein, there is a lack of heat apparent; and it is foolish to lance this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and in the groins and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.

Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and also that which is at the top, and in the case of inflammation of the artery, make an incision through the skin; then work with the lancet as needed, and separate the artery from the veins properly, until it is uncovered; then insert beneath it a needle, and make it pierce to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then stitch the place between the two threads with a probe until the pus comes out which is there, and let the abscess be released; then apply the cure of compresses as long as the threads remain; then follow the care of dressings corresponding to this, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the cutting of the vein, it is necessary that you take in your hand whatever you can of the abscess from all the skin, then insert the needle beneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and let there be a double thread, so that you draw it out from the other side; then tie off the abscess, as I have told you, with one of the two threads of the filament to each of the two sides of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then insert another needle all along one thread beneath all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and constrict the threads in four places; then lance the abscess until the excess comes out, then lance the superfluous part of the skin and leave what is tied off; then place a cloth moistened with wine and oil on top, then administer cures of bandages and dressings until it is healed.

Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: câ€™est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiÃ©s de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui nâ€™ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu lâ€™escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se câ€™est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu lâ€™escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, quâ€™il nâ€™aerse derechief.	 The caustic helps in two ways together: that is, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the glans of the penis is corrupt and retracted, then you must insert into the passage of the penis a reed made of lead, and let the patient urinate through it; and when there is hair on the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, if this occurs due to injury or an abscess, then you must scrape with one instrument until the foreskin is loosened, and the glans of the penis is freed from all sides; and if it is difficult to treat this, then you should scrape with one spatula a small amount from the head of the penis and the skin; then separate gently between two, and place there a subtle cloth of linen soaked in cold water, so that it does not adhere again.
de la circoncision	 of the circumcision
Circoncision nâ€™est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work voluntarily and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the lightest for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il nâ€™en usent mie en lor loi, et nâ€™en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for it is not practiced in their law, and we have acquired nothing from this except what we have learned through experience.
Car jâ€™ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 For I have seen the greatest part of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around I Dal (or Edal), and on the foreskin, and on all the glans; the heart fled because there are two skins, and by chance if one cuts that which is above, the other below remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal nâ€™est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de lâ€™ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront lâ€™uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi quâ€™il nâ€™ont mestier de mundification et je lâ€™ai veut.	 Or there is swelling, and the pain is doubled; and at the amputation of the nail, the point of the member is not secure; and at the amputation of the finger, perhaps the iron slips, and it runs the work, and many times it happens that they do not need amputation, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de lâ€™experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 Of the amputation made at the joints, I have found the effectiveness of the experiment, for the saw cuts exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser lâ€™enfant, sâ€™il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiÃ©s de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de lâ€™ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet dâ€™un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car câ€™est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit dâ€™un moieuf dâ€™uef cuit destempreit dâ€™aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus juscâ€™a lâ€™autre jor, et le cure dâ€™autre cure tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 Because when you press your hand and cut equally in every direction all the time; but let the thread be well twisted around the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child, if he understands, think that you are only tying the thread around the stick; then comfort him in all the ways you can; then hold the stick upright between your hands, and re-tie the threads between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the stick and blow into the heart, and pull it up until the head of the stick is inside; then clean it well of the excrement that has gathered there, then tie the place tightly with a double thread, then tie it under another bandage; and hold it by the second loop with the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two threads, then quickly raise the heart and pull out the head of the stick; then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the best; and put powder on it and on top of the powder a piece of cloth glued with a yolk of cooked egg tempered with rose water, boiled well and fresh, and leave it until the next day, and cure it with other cures until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiÃ©s soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiÃ©s ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The shape of strength for purification is this: the two heads should be sharp and cutting, and the heads should be as large as the palms equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a lâ€™incision; donques il covient que tu lâ€™estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The error in purification is when the heart inside follows the incision; therefore, it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, so that the place does not form an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with pincers, and then cut.
Et sâ€™il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et lâ€™escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if they exceed three days, and what is under the foreskin is swollen, then leave it until the abscess has subsided, and lightly scrape off the scab; cut as much as you can move, and be careful not to cut into the foreskin, for this will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et sâ€™on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 Treat therefore the place of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatment of powders, and if you cut into the heart more than necessary and it goes beyond, it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de lâ€™urine	 Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de lâ€™urine si est dâ€™opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine nâ€™est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbÃ©s sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides sâ€™alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a lâ€™expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et sâ€™elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout lâ€™estrument qui est apelez Â«siringueÂ», de coi ci est li forme: et soit dâ€™argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne dâ€™un oiseil; et soit li caine dâ€™une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to the formation of stones, or congealed blood, or a bone, or living flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone being in the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be seated on their knees; and his feet must be placed on his back, and he should extend his belly on the part above the back, and the patient should hold his breath as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to expel the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which this is the form: and let it be made of fine silver, very light and slender like a bird's feather; and let its tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be slender at the tip.
Et li maniere de lâ€™issue de lâ€™urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute juscâ€™au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue dâ€™oile ou de burre et dâ€™aubin dâ€™uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge dâ€™oile moiste et dâ€™oile dâ€™olive et dâ€™aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant quâ€™elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant juscâ€™a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir juscâ€™a la chose vuide, et ceu nâ€™est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis lâ€™estrai fuer, et fai corre lâ€™urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the issue of the urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie to its end a bag of wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and place it up to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and rinse the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then lightly insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis over towards the scrotum; then advance the syringe into the bladder, and the patient will feel it coming to the empty place, and that is not done according to this order unless because the conduit in which it goes is twisted; then draw out the thread along with all the wool bag by bag, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and let the urine flow; and continue with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout lâ€™estrument qui est apellÃ© Â«clepsedreÂ», et câ€™est li forme:	 When there are scratches or blood in the bladder, or when there is an accumulation of pus, and you want to distill water and medicines into it, then use the entire instrument that is called "clepsydra", and this is its shape:

In this way, you will draw the moisture into the catheter, and then push the tube firmly back inside; the moisture will enter, and will now come to the bladder, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the shape of the subtle enema for enema-ing the bladder: here it is:
Et est dâ€™argent ou dâ€™archaut, et est li chiÃ©s plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment dâ€™un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu nâ€™as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues dâ€™oile et de moistor et dâ€™aigue, et le lie en lâ€™estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie. de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et lâ€™estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briÃ©ment.	 We have already said in the division the ways of stone and its extraction along with medicines; and I have spoken of the difference between rain-induced stones, and all the signs, and on which stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et câ€™est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusquâ€™il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui lâ€™ont petite.	 I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign when urine comes out of the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and there is blood, and the patient's penis hurts, and he often has to urinate, and then it stops; and many of these episodes cause weakness; and the healing of children is light until they are four years old, and it is very serious for the elderly, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those with a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 Et quand nous arrivons au traitement, il faut d'abord purifier le malade par lavement, afin de retirer toute la matiÃ¨re fÃ©cale dans les intestins.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 Because it sometimes happens in seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en lâ€™espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and lift them up and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes comes out from above; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and let his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then seek it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et sâ€™elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice dâ€™oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si lâ€™amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier. Et comande au ministre quâ€™il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande quâ€™il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend the testicles upwards with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the testicles in the place where one makes the cut; then push the spatula carefully, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adÃ©s ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si quâ€™ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, quâ€™elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches quâ€™il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griÃ©s a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make an incision between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the thigh; and let it be straight on the stone, and your two fingers should be on the anus, and let the width of the incision be wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure of the finger in the anus will cause it to come out without difficulty; and know that there is such a stone which has angles and edges: it is difficult to come out; and there is such which is below, similar to a hazelnut, and round, from which the exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et sâ€™elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si quâ€™elle nâ€™eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbÃ© au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si lâ€™estrainche de vitriole; et sâ€™il i a plus dâ€™une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprÃ©s sâ€™il en i a plusors.	 To those with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must use tweezers similar to a file at the top, to gradually squeeze the stone until it does not escape; or insert a subtle instrument bent at the tip below; and if you cannot trick it this way, then widen the pouch at the opening, and if the flesh is torn, constrict it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first push the largest into the bladder neck, then cut above, then pull it out forcefully, and afterwards the smaller ones if there are several.
Et sâ€™elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, then you must cauterize it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adÃ©s par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie tâ€™efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie dâ€™encens et dâ€™aloe et de sanc de dragon, et lâ€™estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier lâ€™aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien juscâ€™au tier jor. Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the bladder, and lodged within, and urine cannot pass; then the treatment for this, as I say, is that you cut it many times, so that it is excused from cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take an iron instrument according to this shape, and let it be fixed with three prongs on one point:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si quâ€™ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant quâ€™il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere dâ€™autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 then take a thread and tie it around the bladder below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then push the instrument into the bladder gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the instrument in the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce through the other side of the stone; then urine will come out immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the bladder.

If it breaks immediately, and urine is ejected with it, then the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this because of any obstacle, tie one thread under the stone and another on top, then insert the penis into the hole between the two threads, then draw out the stone, and untie the string, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	 of a woman's bladder stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et sâ€™il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: lâ€™une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est câ€™on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 It happens rarely that a woman has a bladder stone, and when it does happen, the cure is difficult and is prevented by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled midwife who reveals herself to doctors, especially when she is chaste.

For this happens many times, and let the pus remain until it drains on its own; and if it delays in falling out, then sprinkle with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it drains; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	 of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	 In this case, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent quâ€™ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprÃ©s la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure lâ€™aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done like the hernia which is together with the bladder, in such a manner that you tie the vessels after cutting above lightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess as we have described, until the vessel falls out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et sâ€™il en i dessent, câ€™est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie sâ€™il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par lâ€™estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que lâ€™ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout lâ€™un et lâ€™autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne nâ€™estendre lâ€™uef nâ€™autre chose, si com je tâ€™ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 When a hernia occurs in the inguinal region, as we have said, it opens up the place; and let no one touch the intestines, and if they do, that's bad, and it heals within hours; and yet if it stays too long in this state, the wound or inflammation swells so much that the intestine comes out; and this happens due to the expansion of the inflammation in the inguinal region, as we have said, because it is expanded, then the place becomes softened and swollen and open; and the cure for this is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured with an iron in this manner: and that is for the patient to lie on their back between your hands, then cut the inflamed place of the hernia broadly according to the width of three fingers; and then extract the inflammation that is beneath the skin as usual, then take the reed and place it on the apparent place of the inflammation; and press it deeply into the stomach, then sew the two apparent places of the inflammation onto the head of the reed, and sew both together; then extract the head of the reed, and do not cut or extend anything from the inflammation or other thing, as I have told you in the cure for the hernia of the intestines; then heal it by the healing of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant quâ€™elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, so cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et nâ€™a point dâ€™apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	 The syphilis is constricted, and there is no appearance in the suture, and the cautery is moved to this place, and it is closer to health.
de lâ€™amollissement dou cuir des coions	 of the softening of the leather of the kid
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, câ€™on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant quâ€™il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	 Many times the leather of the kid is softened in some men, because the hairs that are within are softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and one cuts the softened leather onto the natural leather; then sew together the two lips with a stitch, and if you wish, first sew firmly the superfluity of the softened leather at three or four stitches; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as the other wounds until it is healed, and let the thread fall off.
dou chastrement	 From the castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je nâ€™en parlasse mie en cest livre; et nâ€™est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont lâ€™une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement dâ€™aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et dâ€™autres bestes.	 Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore it pleases me not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the physician knows how to respond when asked about it, and knows how to treat it; and the other, because we often have need of castrating some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, I say that castration is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant quâ€™il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the way we do by attraction, make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then take them in your hand, so that they are removed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a lâ€™atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant quâ€™ele soit sanee.	 Of castration of the bull: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspension, and cut on each testicle at I time, when you have well bled them; and leave some pouches of fat and the subtle fat that is above the vessels; and this method of castration is better than that done by attraction, because in attraction there may remain accidentally something of the testicles, which causes the beast to desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	 Of hermaphrodites:
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: lâ€™une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature dâ€™une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways in men: one is such that between the two testicles there appears as if by the figure of a woman's nature, where it has hair, and sometimes urine comes out from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is in women, and let it hang on the wrist like a rod and two ells long.
Et li cure de lâ€™ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si nâ€™a point de cure.	 And the treatment for men and women is to cut the flesh close together, and treat it as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine comes out through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	 Of the tonsils
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant quâ€™elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes lâ€™ont ausi grant com une main, et câ€™est li cure.	 The tonsil is a piece of flesh on the natural part, as long as it is too unsightly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et nâ€™aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc nâ€™i viegne, puis le cure dâ€™autre cure tant quâ€™il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et lâ€™emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance dâ€™une kowe, et por ceu lâ€™apelerent li ancien Â«maladie koweeÂ».	 It is necessary that you take the excess of the tonsil in your hand or with tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, so that bleeding does not come out, then treat it as other wounds until it heals; and for another flesh that grows at the corner of the mouth, and inflames, and perhaps protrudes strongly, and is like the shape of a cow, and therefore the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant quâ€™elle soit sanee.	 Si it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	 of the tendon
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme nâ€™est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou câ€™est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espÃ©s, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et lâ€™enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not open, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that has come; or it is by charm approached, or by subtle or thick sperm, and it is done deeply in the womb, or on the sides, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having children; and knowledge of this is through the examination of the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the swelling appears close to the surface, it should be drawn towards your two fingers or the thumb.
Sâ€™il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si quâ€™il ne puist souder.	 If it is from subtle syphilis, and it is near the II liver, hasten and do thus: put your two fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, with her legs spread; then extend the II liver very much, until the subtle syphilis is round, and cover the swelling; then take wool, and wet it in oil, and put it on the place, and have the woman lie at home each day, so that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espÃ©s, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the syphilis is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a lâ€™oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun dâ€™uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez dâ€™autres cures tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 If the swelling is from flesh-born, then suspend it to a hook and cut it; and have the bleeding medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with plenty of egg; then bring a wide lead plate, so that the wound cannot heal; and let it be thus for a long time, and let him bring a tent of dry linen; then let him be treated with other treatments until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce nâ€™est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when in the flesh comes a new growth, then it should be covered in this manner, unless it is an incarcerated abscess.
Car a lâ€™aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For in an incarcerated abscess that is in the flesh, one should not touch or make it with fire.
des emorroides	 of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances dâ€™aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are accustomed to be without skin, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become swollen; and we have already said in the division their similarities, and their signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il nâ€™aperent au sentir, si nâ€™est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and the swollen ones, when they are completely in the flesh and do not protrude to the touch, then the cure is not by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, câ€™on puet sentir, sont cil câ€™on puet curer.	 Those who are at the mouth of the wound, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent lâ€™altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et dâ€™escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine dâ€™orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then stop the flow with tongs, and cut to its roots, then sprinkle on blood-staunching medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then soak her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is further bleeding, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rinds and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make one plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, câ€™est boin.	 And if he faints, it is good.
