If not, have him draw blood with cupping glasses on the back and breasts without wounding; then take wool, and wet it in plantain juice or juniper juice with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu dâ€™oignement tant quâ€™il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee Â«albathirÂ» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com jâ€™ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess rests, treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and looks like a sharp needle, you must cover it as I have said for the telul; and then treat until it is healed. etti
des apostemes de la marris	 and abscesses of the breast
Maintes manieres dâ€™aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que jâ€™ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscess come to the breast, such as cancer and pustular abscess and herpes and styes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier lâ€™aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui nâ€™est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir lâ€™ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en lâ€™encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et sâ€™il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is necessary therefore that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes in the limbs, which is not one of the abscesses that boils over; and if you want to know the work of iron, look at whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien dâ€™un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre lâ€™estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprÃ©s vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondetÃ© de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de lâ€™estrument nâ€™i viegne plus em parfont quâ€™il ne doit, et quâ€™il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient quâ€™il mette le cornet de lâ€™estrument au desus, et quâ€™il teigne lâ€™estrument.	 Therefore, do not hurry to pierce, but let the matter mature until the pain is soothed; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and there should be two small seats where he leans back, and support his back and draw up his feet to the sides of the thigh; and let his thighs be spread, and have him put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then have him lean toward the left side, and bring there the instrument with which one works on the mouth of the limb, from which later comes the form; and it is necessary that when you want to bring this instrument, you first insert the rod to know the depth of the limb, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the limb with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprÃ©s II jors dâ€™oignement avenant a ceu, tant quâ€™il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere dâ€™aigue et de miel, et puis dâ€™aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a lâ€™oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and one makes an incision with the hand gently, it is necessary to cover it at the head with spongy white cloth; and when the boil is emptied, it is necessary that you put on the wound tents moistened in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the tent outside of the wound on the bottom of the bandage, and place over the bandage and on the arm clean linen moistened in water where mallows are boiled; then cure after two days of ointment according to this, until it is healed; and sometimes one lifts the bandage and the wound with a clister of water and honey, and then with water where long lily roots and aristolochia are boiled; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is on the face, then you must be careful not to burn with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section [on wounds of the face].
de lâ€™enfantement	 of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile quâ€™elle conoisse la figure de lâ€™enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer lâ€™ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the sign is when you see the woman pressing downward and desiring to smell a fragrance: then hasten, for the infant wishes to come out; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, then it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the infant comes out quickly; for when it descends under its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the woman is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleaning; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiÃ©s, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile quâ€™elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse dâ€™error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Because it sometimes occurs on the feet, and comes upon the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes on the stomach, or the back, and is sometimes converted by chance onto the neck, and other evil shapes; thus, it is necessary for the nurse to be wise and skillful in these things, and to guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures of how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature dâ€™oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	 If the child comes out of its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, where women hold her; and let her nature rise with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then the nurse puts between her teeth the small spatula of which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et sâ€™il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant lâ€™enfes.	 And cut the secondine, and slice at its root until the moisture that is within comes out; and hold the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then one must administer a clyster to the woman with fenugreek muscillage with sesame oil; then make her hold and sneeze from condurreth, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus the child will now be expelled.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et sâ€™elles nâ€™i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piÃ©s en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, quâ€™elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains nâ€™i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai lâ€™enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out too strongly, then you must gently push them back little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and raise her feet high; then topple the stool onto the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall during this; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife previously mentioned, and extract the child, and likewise push them back.
de lâ€™issue de lâ€™enfant sus ses piÃ©s	 The issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant quâ€™il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et lâ€™estende poc et poc. Et sâ€™il nâ€™ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant quâ€™il soit selonc la figure natureil.	 And if he does not jump further as we have said, then turn him little by little until he is according to the natural form.

Et sâ€™il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant. If it is perforated to the junction of the thigh, then the tent comes as far as the place; if there is no twisting and the invention of pain around it, it is that it always runs out, and neither medicine nor ointment for healing avails; and in these perforating fistulas there is no cure except labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui nâ€™est mie persans et nâ€™est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com jâ€™ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente dâ€™arain, ou de plonc sâ€™il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In that which is not perforating and is not old, there is hope of health through iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he raises his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent of bronze, or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente lâ€™ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches quâ€™elle est persans; si nâ€™i travillier mie câ€™on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger there, if you then feel that the tent has been pierced; and if it is exposed where you feel between your finger the sphincter or the flesh, then know that it is perforated; do not worry about it for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie câ€™on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide câ€™on i fait, si est câ€™on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant quâ€™il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne dâ€™oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure dâ€™oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 Nevertheless, it is said that one can heal some, but this happens rarely; and the aid given to them is such that one heats a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was previously mentioned; and insert it hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the anus; and do this two or three times, so that you know that these fatty tissues are burnt, which resemble a bird's feather; and then cure the moist tents with butter, until those fats come out, then cure the burning wound with ointment, char and sutures.
Sâ€™il est ensi sanez, câ€™est bien.	 If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce juscâ€™au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des lâ€™encomencement de la fistule, et boute adÃ©s avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprÃ©s, tant quâ€™il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivrÃ© li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne dâ€™oisel, et nâ€™en remaigne niant.	 If so, otherwise it cannot be healed; and if the tent is within, and does not pierce through to the bone at its base, and there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering of the head; then cut off from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward continuously, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and fall out; then clean those fleshy parts that resemble a bird's feather, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et lâ€™uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	 And if the pus overcomes you, and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or strong medicine.

Car the fire cautery combines two good things: namely, the scorching of these hairs adjacent to each other, and the stoppage of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat wet tents with butter or crushed herbs until the place swells, and the burnt hairs are exuded in the swelling; then cure the wound with hardening plasters that contain dry matter, and these medicines are dry.

If you feel the tent and there are two: either the linen or silk thread, or the hair, if it is close to perforating, there should be nothing outside but a path of confidence and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it all the way down, or if you can put tents in it and cure it like before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the support that holds the anus, and the excretion comes out unintentionally; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that covering and clean it after it is cut near the anus, either by tent or by another suitable instrument; then clean the faulty hair in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and keep the fistula in the part outside the anus: this will be a lighter burden for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you insert the tent into the fistula, which is on the side of the foundation near the leather above, then take a pierced tent at the top according to this form:

des emorroydes	 hemorrhoids

There are two types of hemorrhoids: those inside the anus, like grains of resin, both small and large, from which blood always flows, whether there is one or many, and they protrude from the anus and at the opening of the anus; but those that protrude have little moisture, and always have a little yellow water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh. The cure for those who have them inside the anus is to command the patient to sit to pass stool in the chambers until the anus issues forth, and the threads appear; then hasten and seize it with tongs, or hold it with your nail, then cut off its roots; and if the nails cannot hold it because of its moisture, then take it with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camlet; and pull with your fingers, then cut, and sprinkle some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or cauterize as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure with other cures until healed. And if the anus cannot issue forth, then enema the patient with a biting and harsh enema to clean what is in the anus so that it may issue out clearly. When the patient sits and the threads come forth from the anus, the cure is light; and it is that you seize them with your nail or tongs, and cut, then cure as we have said, until healed, and let him fear incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier lâ€™aguille dâ€™autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz lâ€™aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai lâ€™aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide kâ€™il repose; et puis le laisse tant quâ€™il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure dâ€™oignement et dâ€™autre cure, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 If you must bring the seam according to this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it into a needle, then draw the thread through the top and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two heads of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; and tighten the thread strongly, then tie a knot in the thread, and pull out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one for draining the blood; then place on top a small moistened cloth with rose oil or with wax, and place on top, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they have healed, and when they are healed, cure them with unguent and other cures, so that they may heal.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	 Of dryness of the bowel at the foundation

dou fremit	 Of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 An ant is a small creature that walks upon the body and goes very deep; sometimes it meets cold, and one feels it also like a trembling death, and it comes over the whole body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne dâ€™une penne dâ€™oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the treatment is such that you take a quill from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place this quill on the trembling area until the circle completely surrounds the trembling area; then turn your hand all around the quill so that it covers the entire trembling area, and insert it deeply, and cleanse the trembling area of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu dâ€™une caine dâ€™arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you see, then do this with a quill of bronze or iron in this manner, and let it be subtle below and sharp above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 nor should it be perceived, to hold the two together and press them more. And if you see, then cauterize the trembling area as it is before in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 about the form of the enema

des plaies	 Wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc lâ€™acomplissement.	 We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the section on division; now we will tell you about treatments for hands and medications, according to their uses.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu quâ€™elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to what caused them, and according to the places where they are located, and by what means they were inflicted.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille dâ€™espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are inflicted are by the blow of a stone, and cut of sword or knife, or spear or stick or arrow, or similar things; and according to the places on the body where they occur, such as wound that falls upon the neck, or head, or chest, or belly, or liver, and similar members. And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, beginning with simple head wounds, because their treatment will come in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os nâ€™est brisiez, si pren garde se câ€™est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement dâ€™aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement sâ€™il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os nâ€™est brisiez, si pren garde se câ€™est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement dâ€™aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement sâ€™il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.
Et sâ€™il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et sâ€™il nâ€™i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, sâ€™elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle nâ€™est muee par lâ€™air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprÃ©s; et se li ars lâ€™ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if he does not wish to be healed, let his food be diminished, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and place on the wound, if an abscess comes there, cotton soaked in rose oil alone, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the fresh wound, while all its blood remains, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will describe a little later; and if the fire has moved it, place some ointments on it, until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure dâ€™espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be closed by stitches, then close them by suture, as I will say for wounds of the belly, regarding sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de lâ€™os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed bone, and it gapes, and holds only by a thread, then cut [it]; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as turnips and cooked wheat, likewise onions, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il nâ€™aert a lâ€™os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier lâ€™artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie dâ€™un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find decay in the skin that reaches to the bone, then cut all the decay away, and cast it out, then cure [it]; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which the blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then search for the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help at all, then cauterize [it].
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars lâ€™ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light; and it is that you put in this powder that heals before the heat has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et lâ€™estraint forment, tant quâ€™elle sâ€™aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, sâ€™elle nâ€™enfle; car on nâ€™oste la madicine tant quâ€™ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and fill the wound, and press it strongly, until it heals well and unites with all its flesh; and then bind it well, and leave it without untying, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on nâ€™ait lâ€™encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars nâ€™ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this with only quicklime, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but the heat must move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si nâ€™i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine dâ€™orge faites dâ€™aigue et de miel, tant quâ€™ele giete bowe; puis le cure dâ€™autres cures tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if the ars has moved the wound, even in the summer, do not put any of this powder on it; but put on some cooked ointments, or poultices made from barley flour with water and honey, until it casts pus; then proceed with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure dâ€™os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si lâ€™estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprÃ©s les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then draw it out with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	 of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si nâ€™a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee. des vils	 of the fingers

This illness is called in our land "illness of the ox," because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and it goes through the whole body ascending and descending, and one feels it well as it moves from limb to limb until it reaches the skin where it goes, and it comes out; and it is engendered by the putrefaction of some humors, just like worms and serpents and leeches and ascarids in the belly; and one fears its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.

When you see it being cured and drawn out, one cannot force it except when it goes: so it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong binding tightly, then cut on top and draw strongly, and if the pus is deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire on top until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it can run into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head of the eye, tightly bind below it the sorcil, then cut on top, and draw strongly; and the patient must use a cleansing of the body with solvent medicines for bad humors, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.

Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne dâ€™enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant quâ€™elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre. Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren lâ€™estrument qui est apelez Â«fosseurÂ», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for redness; and its quality is such that the patient should twist his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur," which has this shape:

Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en lâ€™espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne nâ€™apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et nâ€™aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et câ€™est li forme dou flaime:	 The bleeding of the vein of the nose helps against fever and insanity and diseases of the face such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bloodletting is such that the patient should twist his neck, then press his nose with your left hand, and take a subtle long flame, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind for one night, because it is quickly healed; and this is the shape of the flame:

de la sainie des leivres	 of the liver bleeding

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie nâ€™est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en lâ€™une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: câ€™est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en lâ€™encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprÃ©s mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprÃ©s II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you must know about bleeding is that bleeding is only introduced for the sake of maintaining health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins which are: cephalic, basilic or fast; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring, autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and one should bleed on the first day or third, two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies nâ€™a point dâ€™oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans juscâ€™a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois juscâ€™a septime. Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 One should not bleed those who have passed sixty years of age.

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et sâ€™il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses. Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 And often there is an abscess and swelling at the cauterization of the basilica: therefore place your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft upon the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de lâ€™artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure dâ€™autre cure, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 When it happens that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for by chance some comes out of the artery; but make a dry poultice to strengthen the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw from each according to the quantity of its power and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant quâ€™il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant quâ€™il soit subtiliiez; et sâ€™il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes fine; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier dâ€™estraction de sanc, câ€™on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the one who is robust and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and that the flame be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and bleed him little by little and often, and he should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from loss of blood and from cutting the nerve, and it is worth more than long or broad bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; sâ€™il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et sâ€™il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzÃ©, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And to the one whose body lacks blood, one must give wet bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, then draw out blood three or four times. And if he has a cold temperament, then before bleeding, eat wet bread soaked in muscadine syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et sâ€™il paume a la sainie, aprÃ©s lâ€™issue de mout de sanc, si covient quâ€™il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por lâ€™evacuation de voinne.	 And if he faints during bleeding, after losing much blood, he should smell broth of meat and fragrant, subtle syrup, and use other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et sâ€™il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, kâ€™il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wants to bleed from the arm and heal at other times, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he be bled a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprÃ©s la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprÃ©s la premiere sainie, ou aprÃ©s la nuevime houre.	 And if he wants to bleed from the arm after the first bleeding and he has a strong body, then let him be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier dâ€™autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And if he wants to bleed from another part, then he should bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant quâ€™il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne sâ€™il est corbes, quâ€™il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant quâ€™il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 Because there is much blood within the body that has already heated up and causes fever; therefore, one must draw out a large quantity and widen the opening until it flows like a fountain; after you have checked all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on his pulse when he bleeds, so that death does not come in place of the fountain, and this often happens when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not necessary, when you see the arm being released and blood coming out a second time and the opening is closed, to press hard; nor if it is crooked, should he extend his arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until it bleeds a second time; or you can prick with the point of the flame, so that the frozen blood at the vein's mouth may flow out, and place on I poultice of linen dipped in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne lâ€™estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it at all until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en lâ€™autre bras.	 And if there is a need to draw blood a second time, then heal it in the same place or in another vein or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu quâ€™elle est composte.	 The veins in the arm are healed in the place of the chief vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiÃ©z moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans nâ€™en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en lâ€™aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se câ€™est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on lâ€™i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, quâ€™il nâ€™i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of the healing is such that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the little finger turns red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well; then heal it now crosswise, not widely or lengthwise; and let the hole be large, and heal it very close to the joint of the hand; and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the healing of this vein is safer than any other veins, because there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et câ€™est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si câ€™on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et nâ€™aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et nâ€™en puet issir.	 Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie,
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier tâ€™est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn out as much blood as is necessary, then put oil and seal on the vein to close it quickly, and do this for each time.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je tâ€™ai dit devers destre.	 The bleeding from the left hand is good for the disease of the spleen, and do the same as I have told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The bleeding from the ankle is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the stomach, retention of blood, kidney disease, and old hip and leg diseases, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant quâ€™elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient should put their foot in hot water, and rub on the vein until it opens, and tie around the ankle joint of the foot; and the veins are at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins; bleed then in the widest vein or at the ankle, for that is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are below, and make the incision crosswise like a cup; and let the flame be calm.
Et se li sans nâ€™en puet issir, si remet lou piet en lâ€™aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and leave it to bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de lâ€™autre piet igalment.	 And if the blood does not come out the first time, then start again the second time a little higher, because the place is salty; do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the vein of the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant câ€™est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic vein is on the ankle of the foot, and its bleeding relieves hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement nâ€™apert li voinne; et sâ€™elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 Et la qualitÃ© de sa saignÃ©e est telle que le malade entre dans un bain, et il fait tourner au-dessus de la cheville quatre doigts en les tordant, car sinon la veine ne s'ouvre pas; et si elle s'ouvre, alors tu la saignes de toutes les maniÃ¨res que tu peux, et en traversant; et il vaut mieux que tu coupes le lieu, car l'endroit est sec, et elle est trÃ¨s rÃ©pandue chez de nombreuses personnes.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et lâ€™estraint; ele est maintenant sanee. des sainies de ventouse	 of bleeding with a cupping glass
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou dâ€™arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 Cupping glasses are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu nâ€™en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie quâ€™elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cupping which is without striking is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and the cupping which is done by striking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places of the body, one of which is entirely on top of the head; and another is on the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; and a cupping under the chin; and a cupping on both shoulders; and a cupping on the buttocks; and cupplings in both arms; and cupplings in both legs; and cupplings in both ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood, except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for that reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with venous bleeding; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si lâ€™amenistrons chescune houre en lâ€™encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness one must perform bloodletting, or by custom, we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, and at the end, and in the middle, and in all times; for there are such people who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head; and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in the eyes; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and vomit blood; and there are those who dream, and see in their sleep bloody and wounded and dead things and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant câ€™est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprÃ©s III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order them to be bled after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief â€¦ que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprÃ©s lâ€™evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The bleeding from the nose also helps with the dizziness of the head â€¦ that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this evacuation is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic, and those who are of cold complexion should not use it, or who have catarrh, because it does great harm to them; and therefore the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui sâ€™en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance dâ€™obliance.	 And those who frequently bleed from it become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of becoming forgetful.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a lâ€™estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car sâ€™elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The cupping in the neck is in place of the bleeding from the head and the basilica, and therefore it is useful for the constriction of the bladder, and for splitting the vein of the arm, and for jaundice, and for repletion; and there one should bleed a little, because if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness in the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a lâ€™estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor quâ€™il espresse sa main au mettre, quâ€™il ne cope lâ€™artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosations at the two ribs of the neck are good for headaches, and for inflammation of the eyes, and for migraines, and for choking, and for toothache, and it is in place of the sinus of the basilica; and you must instruct the patient to press his hand when applying it, so that he does not cut the artery, and that blood does not flow out.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 The ventosations under the chin are good for diseases of the mouth, and for the decay of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the sinuses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 The ventosations of the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor quâ€™il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The incisions of the ribs are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the physician not to strike too deeply inward, for the place is bare of flesh, and beneath lie nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit dâ€™arain, quâ€™elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, sâ€™elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	 The cupping glass on the buttocks is worth as much for hemorrhoids of the anus and diseases below, and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large, and made of copper, so that it draws well; and by chance, if it were fine, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprÃ©s lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 The incisions on the legs heal well, for they draw blood from the whole body and are worth as much for old pains in the sides, and in the loins, and in the bladder, and remove flowers; and they are placed on the two spleens and the two ankles. However, they weaken the body over long use, and bring about paralysis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	 The method of applying the cupping glass is to place it first empty, and suck promptly, and apply quickly, and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the appearance of blood under the skin; then prick, and reapply the cups, and take care in the arrangement of the body, for there are those who have dark flesh and clear pores: it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and one deep puncture; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 And if the flesh is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espÃ©s, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And if the flesh is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, we must be content with just one prick.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espÃ©s, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses dâ€™oile aperitif et dissolutif: se câ€™est en esteit, dâ€™oile violet, ou dâ€™oile dâ€™amandres douces, ou dâ€™oile de semence de cucurbite; et se câ€™est en yveir, dâ€™oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we wish to take much blood, then we bleed often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the end of it should be that the heart may be pierced suddenly. And for those who have thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, you must anoint the places of the cupping glasses with opening and dissolving oil: in summer, with violet oil, or almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and in winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar oils.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile dâ€™anet, et les semblans.	 And if the excess is thick and cold, then take bitter oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se nâ€™i covient mettre point dâ€™oile, mais le covient laver aprÃ©s la ventosation dâ€™aigue rose, ou dâ€™aigue froide, ou dâ€™aigue de morelle, ou dâ€™aigue de cucurbite, ou dâ€™aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one who is healed has tender flesh and large pores, then no oil should be put there, but it must be washed after with rose water, or cold water, or black nightshade water, or cucumber water, or periwinkle water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve dâ€™aisil, ou dâ€™aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And the one who has much moisture should be lifted with ease, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou dâ€™aigue de seuc, ou de decoction dâ€™anet ou de camomile, ou dâ€™autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprÃ©s lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprÃ©s la ventosacion, et covient kâ€™il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have large superfluities should be lifted with old wine, or water of leek, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things; and they must not be healed with cupping before the bath nor during the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and they should not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that they wash themselves when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient quâ€™il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a lâ€™aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And beware if the one who is healing is of a choleric nature, and if his blood is too hot and inflamed; then he must take cold things, such as crab apples and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and he should eat pears, and flesh of goat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor quâ€™il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprÃ©s, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And he who has a cold constitution should take syrup of honey, and medium-scented wine, which is between old and new, and he should eat apple, and pear, and small birds and larks; and on the day that he will bleed himself, then he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or musk before bleeding, or after, to strengthen the main members; and let the blood be subtilized, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure lâ€™opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes dâ€™aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere câ€™on emplisse la ventouse dâ€™aigue chaude soule, ou dâ€™aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The cupping glasses that are placed without piercing are those that are placed on the liver, and on the bladder, and for gout, and on the stomach and the udder and the kidneys and the hip, because these members do not tolerate being pierced over the eyes, and it is only done to attract blood from one member to another, as we place them on the breasts when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the stomach and on the udder to reduce the member; and it relieves pain, when there is a boil or stone, it removes by its attractive power perhaps the boil, or dries the stone from its place; and thus it does when placed on the liver and on the bladder when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cupping glass with only hot water, or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministrÃ© a feu si est ci:	 The shape of the cupping glass administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit dâ€™arain, souef devant si quâ€™ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers dâ€™arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et lâ€™eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on its side around the middle a small hole, just as to insert a needle, and let it be of tin, smooth on the inside so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle, let there be a crossbar of tin or iron to hold a lit candlewick, both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who use them, for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the elderly, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse quâ€™elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one should thus place this cupping glass on the limb: take a candlewick of wax or linen and insert it into the middle of the cupping glass along the crossbar that is inside the cupping glass, so that the light is at the bottom of the cupping glass to prevent it from burning the patient; then place it on the limb, and your two fingers should be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wants, the vapor will escape, and remove the cupping glass; and take another candlewick as before, and repeat it often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, nâ€™a point de verge ne de pertus, et nâ€™est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine dâ€™aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et câ€™est li forme:	 In the cupping glass used for pleurisy, there is no rod or hole, and it is only prepared when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb alone; this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de lâ€™user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant quâ€™elles soient famillouses, et nâ€™aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant kâ€™il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se câ€™est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprÃ©s.	 Sleeveworms are only prepared for use in small members where cups cannot be applied due to their size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in fleshless areas, such as fingers or noses, and other similar ones; and the quality of their use is such that when you find leeches that are in clean water without filth, take them; and put one in clean water until they are accustomed to it, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then let it be bloodletting with a vein and a cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cup can be applied, apply it, for this is very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu dâ€™aisil, et puis dâ€™aigue, mout bien, et puis lâ€™espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprÃ©s lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiÃ©s; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broiÃ©, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant quâ€™il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant quâ€™elles sâ€™aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, then lift the place of ease with water, very well, and then apply pressure; and if the place is too wet after the leeches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply until the blood is drawn out; and if the blood is plentiful, apply crushed vitriol or gall nuts, and similar things, until it is drawn out; or you can put half of peeled beans on the place, and leave them until they dry on the place, it will stop bleeding now; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si sâ€™aerdent; et quant tu vues quâ€™elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc dâ€™aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the leeches do not want to attach, rub the place with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the blood comes out, and then apply the leeches, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are falling off, sprinkle some powdered aloe and burned seaweed, or ash, and they will fall off now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	 Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en lâ€™art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	 This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is for the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, quâ€™il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre nâ€™en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je nâ€™en trovai onques nul boin; et nâ€™en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou jâ€™ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par lâ€™acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et lâ€™ai abregiÃ© en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com jâ€™ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that the foolish physicians cast away this chapter because they never saw any of the ancient books nor read any letter from them; and for this reason science is foreign in our land, for I never found a good one; and I do not know anything about it except through the knowledge of the ancient books where I have studied so much that I acquired the knowledge, and by experience, and by the practice of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained in them, and abbreviated at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et lâ€™aprenent a autrui.	 It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide dâ€™une part et dâ€™autre, sâ€™aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens nâ€™est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, câ€™est a savoir froides joutes, et char dâ€™oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne sâ€™emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu nâ€™aies doute dâ€™aposteme chaut, ne dâ€™espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement kâ€™il a useit.	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or sprain or break occurs to anyone, you must hasten to heal the patient on both sides, unless something prevents you completely, such as weakness of the body, infancy, old age; or if the time is not very cold, or too hot; and avoid cold foods, that is to say cold porridge, and bird meat and hare meat, and do not drink wine, and do not eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with too many foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or spreading matter in the limb; then let the patient return to his former regimen.
Et quant li os brisiÃ©s comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	 And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide abundant nourishment, which have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and belly of cow, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	 For with such nourishment the bones mend faster and more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais nâ€™a cure, ramoinne sus lâ€™os brisiet I gros tenrons qui sâ€™aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant quâ€™il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken old and weak bones cannot heal or mend according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too soft, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset the broken bone with a strong tenon that holds the limb together until it regains its strength as before; and if it does not fully recover, then he must be nourished with abundant foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	 And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	 For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille dâ€™une penne por escrire.	 For there is a fracture that goes awry, and another by sharpening, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	 And there is fracture with wound, and fracture which is entirely a small slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de lâ€™os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il nâ€™i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se nâ€™i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each kind has its own device, and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what comes back into place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone because the place is twisted, opens well by force, and sounds on pressing with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound on touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it can well have twisting, or slit, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprÃ©s, et puis lâ€™estraint maintenant subtilment.	 If it is not necessary to move it with your hand, but apply the following medicines and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis lâ€™estraint, si com il covient ci aprÃ©s.	 And know that the fractures that go in the air, and are the two parts disjointed, it is now necessary to set them equally, before an abscess comes there; and if a hot abscess comes there, leave it for some days, until the abscess is appeased; then set it as you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of one where there are pieces; then restrain it, as it will be said later.
Et se en lâ€™os a piÃ©ces brisies, si lâ€™estent de II pars, se câ€™est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se câ€™est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiÃ©s des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if there are pieces broken in the bone, and they are of two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and at your hand; and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, reduce by all means the additions in their places as you can, and beware that through your work no harm or pain comes to the patient; and join well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main sâ€™il te semble kâ€™il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne lâ€™estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 And he can feel it well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then straighten it beautifully, and do not press it too much, nor squeeze as those who cause a hot abscess and contraction of the member through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide quâ€™il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez quâ€™il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the member is healed, instruct the patient well that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and make sure that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si nâ€™est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition quâ€™il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde kâ€™il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez nâ€™i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when he feels any pain, it is not yet healed, and it must be put in such a position that he feels no pain; and ensure that it is set straight, so that twisting does not occur when it has been restored; and the qualities of the broken member are as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	 Know that broken limbs vary in smallness and largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir dâ€™un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et lâ€™estraint de toutes pars igalment, si quâ€™il nâ€™i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et lâ€™estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et lâ€™estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant quâ€™il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, sâ€™il nâ€™i a aposteme ou enfleure.
