For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large limb, and tighten from all sides equally, so that there is no gap; then tie light wool around, III or IV times according to the limb, and tighten the hand a little on the whole bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break is separated by a little from the break; and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy place, then take another bandage, and turn around again on the broken place; then go back to the lower part of the break, and tighten moderately, not too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first wrap above; then put wool or cloth between the bandages, so that they are all equal, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then place your splints well on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et sâ€™il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste lâ€™enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet dâ€™une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or an abscess, place on it something that soothes the abscess and removes the swelling, and leave it thus for some days; then draw up your supports, and let them be of half the width of a large cane, made wisely, or of wood from which clives are made, or of palm leaves, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adÃ©s moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com jâ€™ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et câ€™est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal sâ€™il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie quâ€™il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi dâ€™espaice.	 but the support that is placed on the fracture must be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and it should be as long as is necessary for the member in terms of size or length; then place the supports as you did in the first layer, then tie on top a thread evenly, as was done in the first layer on the fracture; tighter at the top, then less so; and the threads must be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and they should be soft linen; for if the threads are thick, like I have seen the foolish people who make their ties from twisted flax, it is a great mistake, because the tie cannot be equal if it is too tight, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each support.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiÃ©s des esteles aprÃ©s lâ€™estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si quâ€™il ne se blece.	 Et si le patient est blessÃ© par les pointes des Ã©toiles aprÃ¨s la compression dans ses veines, alors placez sous elles des bandages de lin ou de laine dÃ©chirÃ©e, afin qu'il ne soit pas blessÃ©.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprÃ©s.	 When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will describe its treatment later.
Et saiches quâ€™il ne covient mie estraindre dâ€™esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	 And know that it is not appropriate to compress all broken members with tourniquets on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se nâ€™i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprÃ©s V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit dâ€™aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun dâ€™uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et câ€™est li commune maniere de lâ€™emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il nâ€™est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 Because when the member is large, it is not appropriate to apply tourniquets unless after five or seven days, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess occurring; and see here the manner of the ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: and that you take flour that stays on the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and put this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, into use, and it is the common way of the plaster restoring the fracture in many positions, especially for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere dâ€™emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren Ð— abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X Ð—.; mirre et aloes, ana V Ð—.; alechil VIIII Ð—.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun dâ€™uef; se li complexion de lâ€™ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiÃ©s hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 Autre maniere dâ€™emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren Ð— abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X Ð—.; mirre et aloes, ana V Ð—.; alechil VIIII Ð—.;
Autre maniere dâ€™emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X Ð—.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII Ð—.; acaice VI Ð—.; bolic armenic X Ð—., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun dâ€™uef, et lâ€™aministre.	 Other method of plaster suitable for torsion: take mugwort and vismalva, ana 10; myrrh and aloes, ana 9; acacia, 6; bolus Armenicum, 10, and grind well, and make a paste with water and abundance of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere dâ€™emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de lâ€™os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of plaster for dislocated joints and displaced bones, and to soothe the pain that follows, and for those who use bone-cutting: take new wool, and soften it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply to the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier dâ€™aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore [the joint], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and properly removes the pains.
Autre maniere dâ€™emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Other method of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground ivy, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere dâ€™emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de lâ€™os et por amenusier lou remenant de lâ€™aposteme.	 Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fracture and to bring out the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou dâ€™aigue, et en use.	 Take roots of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, fava bean flour, one part each; grind them and mix with wine, and if the limb is hot, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere dâ€™emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of plaster, stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of mallow, flax seed, balm, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and camomile; take one part of each; and grind, and make a paste with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre câ€™on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et dâ€™oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist quâ€™il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	 Hippocrates says in his book that for a broken member to restore strength, one should use only an ointment made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between two, not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien câ€™on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	 And it seems that Galen says one should put on a broken member, to restore it, dry things somewhat hot, like myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere dâ€™emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz dâ€™omes decopez, ou pennes dâ€™oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Other method of plaster for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped hazel leaves or bird feathers, add balsam, and salt equally; grind them into a plaster and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprÃ©s, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne sâ€™est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste lâ€™emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur dâ€™aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc dâ€™emplaustre, et ne lâ€™estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And then unbind it a little later, and see if the patient feels no pain, or if the bone has not moved from its place; do not re-bind for many days. And if pain comes to the spot, or itching, lack of rest or swelling, then hasten, and unbind, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and dip in water, and raise the spot until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind with a nut, until you are sure of the warm abscess; and the inflammation of the limb subsides, and the pain is removed, then resume the subtle bandage, and a little plaster, and do not bind as tightly as before; and continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier dâ€™emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	 And if you see that the abscess is red and painful and swollen, and I have removed it all, and you need a poultice and bandage, then start again as you did first.
Et sâ€™il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprÃ©s III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce câ€™on voit, tant que li briseure sâ€™aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com jâ€™ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier nâ€™est, saiches que norrissemens nâ€™i puet venir; arose lou donques dâ€™aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: câ€™est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je nâ€™i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de lâ€™ovrer droitement.	 And if nothing comes to the limb as we have said, then do not unbind it until after three days or four or five or seven; sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what is seen, so that the fracture hardens and the union of the flesh approaches; then bind it tighter than before, and let the flesh swell, as I said earlier; and if you see the place drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; therefore, apply warm tepid water each time you unbind it, every third day, and slightly loosen the bandage; thus this practice brings nourishment to the limb and quickly corrects what foolish doctors do, who bind the limb badly: this is bad, and such practices are dangerous, and I see nothing there but leaving it and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	 Of the various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion dâ€™espee, et li colz oste tout lâ€™os juscâ€™a syfac qui est desoz lâ€™os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure Â«haichureÂ».	 There are many methods of fractures and various shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures that are caused by the blow of a sword, and the bone is completely severed up to the marrow which is under the bone, just as an axe or stake does; and therefore this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope lâ€™os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure Â«absolueÂ»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 If the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this type of fracture is called "absolue"; and the wound caused by these two fractures can be large or small.
Et sâ€™il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou dâ€™autres semblans.	 And if there is a blunt force trauma, or a split from the blow of a stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar causes.
Et sâ€™il a brisure persant, qui aproiche juscâ€™a la toile qui est desoz lâ€™os, ou elle est sus lâ€™os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	 And if there is a piercing fracture, which reaches as far as the flesh beneath the bone or on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en lâ€™os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure Â«capillaireÂ»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de lâ€™os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as thinly as a hair, and the fracture is small, for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is caused by striking with a stone or falling or something similar, and it causes a fragment of bone to enter inside, and the place swells up like when blacksmiths strike on cauldrons; then the bone enters.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief dâ€™enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in the head, as in a child's head; and it occurs in all these types of fractures that small fragments are separated like stars; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et lâ€™inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	 And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the traction upon them, and the inquiry with pins, and by the rotten flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert lâ€™os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	 The appearance of hairline fracture is known because when the bone is exposed and rubbed upon, it reveals the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission dâ€™entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	 In the care of fractures, beware of the patientâ€™s accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, paralysis, fever, or the eyes coming out strong and red, and other similar things in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	 And if you do not see a frightening accident and expect healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et câ€™est en yver, si covient oster lâ€™os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	 And when the wounded person comes to you first, and this is in winter, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day after you can.
Et se câ€™est en esteit, si te haste dâ€™oster lâ€™os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz lâ€™os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	 And if this is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh under the bone does not become corrupt, and the accidents that we have spoken of occur.
Et se li brisure de lâ€™os vient juscâ€™a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus lâ€™os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir lâ€™os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu quâ€™il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor lâ€™os a oster, et câ€™est fait selonc II manieres dâ€™ovraige: lâ€™une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et câ€™est li forme:	 And if the break of the bone reaches to the skin that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part thus: and it is that you take the head of the wounded person, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and more softly on the figure of the wound than you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or an abscess like this, if he helps with what is needed, and it is that you fill the place with bandages soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is appeased, and you are sure of the bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two types of work: one type is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	 And then he applies another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 And the second method is such that you have a variety of cuts, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made of Indian iron; and work lightly so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont quâ€™il ne percent outre lâ€™os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre lâ€™os; et tâ€™en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de lâ€™espÃ©s de lâ€™os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et câ€™est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 And if the bone is out and hard, you must first bore around it before applying cuts with trepans, not so deep that they pierce through the skull; and above the point there should be a rim or circle to prevent the point from piercing through the bone; and you should have several of them, such that each fits in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have trepans for all skulls; and this is the form of the three types of trepans:
Li qualitez por percier entor lâ€™os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus lâ€™os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprÃ©s, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires lâ€™espaice de lâ€™os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies lâ€™os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 The qualities for piercing around a broken bone are that you place the awl on the bone and turn it with your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then place the awl elsewhere a short while after, and do this all around, then cut away with the incision tool the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as subtly and lightly as possible, as we have said, until you draw out the bone in your hand, or with any of the instruments you have such as tongs, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras lâ€™os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses lâ€™apreteit qui est demoree de lâ€™os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient quâ€™il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et sâ€™il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et dâ€™oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, it is necessary to scrape away any remaining fragments of the bone with all other similar instruments like an incision tool, but it should be thinner and more subtle than the other incision tool; and if there remains any small bones or scales, then lightly remove them with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with lint and onions as we have said.
Et li autre maniere dâ€™ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et câ€™est sa parole.	 And the other manner of working is that which Galen said, which is more secure; and he praised it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de lâ€™os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	 It is necessary first that you expose a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to have moved, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place beneath the head of this chisel-like instrument, which has this form:
Et ne trenche mie dâ€™une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers lâ€™os; puis fier dâ€™un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement lâ€™os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; sâ€™elle est aerse a lâ€™os, si lâ€™oste legierement, car on lâ€™oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut from one side only, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly chip the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath; if it is too tight against the bone, loosen it gently, for one can remove it without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de lâ€™os ne perce juscâ€™a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc lâ€™ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	 Et si la fracture osseuse ne perce pas jusqu'Ã  la peau, et que l'os est cassÃ© lÃ©gÃ¨rement par le dessus, avec de petits fragments, alors il faut effacer cette rugositÃ©, et enlever les Ã©cailles Ã  l'aide d'un raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitÃ©s, afin d'ajuster chaque endroit de la maniÃ¨re la plus appropriÃ©e, selon le travail et la forme de la fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprÃ©s de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant kâ€™il soit bien.	 And scrape first with large rasps, and then with finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et câ€™est chose que nâ€™est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 In each of the other delicate incisions and subtle fractures, it is necessary to adjust according to its condition; and this is something that is not granted to one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublÃ© en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne lâ€™estraindre mie fuer que tant kâ€™il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre dâ€™encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adÃ©s medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adÃ©s nette, que tu nâ€™i laissier mie lâ€™oignement, ne nâ€™i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe sâ€™asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the surface is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth, folded in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not burden the surface, then apply another ligature over it, and do not tighten it too much so that it only touches the wound; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess is appeased, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and always apply soothing medicines without irritation; and ensure that the wound is always clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, or allow pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the brain's membrane, it will run and burst, and great harm comes to the patient; for when a stinging substance is placed on the surface, it kills above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	 Take heed therefore, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful indeed.
Et se noiror nâ€™i vient fuers que por la medicine câ€™on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties dâ€™oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures quâ€™il couvient, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if blackness comes about other than from the medicine that has been applied, which may have such power, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and make a plaster of one cloth; then apply it to the wound; then cure it in various ways as needed until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer kâ€™enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 Know that sometimes the two upper parts of the nose are broken, or one alone, for there are two bones there; and the lower one is made of cartilage and does not break, but only swells or turns, and then heals.
Et se lâ€™une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger through the nose hole, and place the break evenly inside your finger, and push out with the thumb, so that the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief dâ€™un rait un poc gros.	 And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach it, then you must place a large clot at the end of a reed evenly.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprÃ©s lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, do the same again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then insert at the end of the nose tenths of linen cloth, if the break is in one part. iÄ™ Et se li brisure est en II parties, si mete par deus entre les dois briseses une petite rait, et les boute ains, tant que les II briseses sâ€™ajointent; et metez sus la rupture une fichue moulee ou une autre chose, pour coi li neis puisse estre droiz. iÄ™ And if the break is in two parts, place between the two breaks a small reed, and push them together until the two breaks join; and place on top of the fracture a cast or another thing, so that the nose may be straight.
Ou tu boutes I autre dâ€™autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses quâ€™eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 Where you push one against another, if there is a fracture there; and let the tendons be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour câ€™on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some say that one should grease the tendons in butter, and change them daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient quâ€™elles soient moillies en confection dâ€™aubun dâ€™uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be greased in a mixture of egg white and ground flour; then leave the tendon until the bone is healed and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes dâ€™oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 And sometimes one puts in the nose goose quills instead of tendons, and then wraps a soft cloth around it, and this holds the fracture together; now do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	 And if such abscesses come to the nose while you are working there, place a poultice of cotton moistened in rose oil, or a little dip in aquiline.
Et se apostemes chaus nâ€™i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre dâ€™encens, confites avec aubun dâ€™uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiÃ©s em menues pieces, si lâ€™estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et sâ€™il nâ€™a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if such abscesses do not come, apply an external poultice of sesame flour and frankincense powder, mixed with egg white, then place light dressings on top; and do not bind the nose. And if the nasal fracture is small and broken into tiny pieces, reduce it using appropriate instruments, then suture the laceration, and treat similar flesh wounds with suitable plasters and ointments; and if there is no internal wound in the nose, treat it with tents, and place lead cannulas until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	 Of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il nâ€™i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et nâ€™est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	 When the jaw is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only inside and not broken in two, but rather splintered within, it is recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et lâ€™afaite a lâ€™autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then insert your right index finger, and gently push the fracture inside, and adjust it from the outside with the other hand, making it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant quâ€™il soit igalz.	 And if the jaw fracture is divided into two, then you must provide traction to both parts until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain dâ€™un fil dâ€™or ou dâ€™argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide quâ€™il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 And if there is movement of the teeth or loosening, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw grease, and place on it a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large well-made cushion, or an equal piece of leather long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it above as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que câ€™est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun dâ€™uef ou farine de sisament, aprÃ©s ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus lâ€™emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres sâ€™aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant kâ€™il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 And if you see that the figure changes, unbind it on the third day, and then reset what has changed; and place a plaster over it, of mill powder with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the grease; and place over the plaster light linen cloth, and if the plaster dries out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	 And if such abscesses occur, then treat them as we have said many times before.
Et sâ€™il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de lâ€™os en est ostee; si subtilie de lâ€™oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine to see if any piece of bone has been removed; then extract it with the appropriate instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si lâ€™eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	 And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il nâ€™i demore nule, si cout la plaie, sâ€™ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, sew up the wound if it is wide, and place on it suitable dressings to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	 of the forearm
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers lâ€™espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 The forearm breaks in several places towards the shoulder, and the fractures are of three types: either it is broken and separated into two parts with pieces in between, which is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne lâ€™ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et nâ€™i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 And the work is such that when the break is without wound, you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken strength; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then place the break equally between your fingers, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz lâ€™espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And if you need to extend more, place under the patientâ€™s shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity; and extend and lift the broken strength, and press the sphere with your hand, so that you equalize the break as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu quâ€™elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz lâ€™espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres lâ€™espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	 And if you cannot pull the head of the broken bone out of the skin because it comes from within, it is necessary that the patient lie on their back, and place under the shoulder a pillow halfway, and the assistant presses the shoulder downward until the bone of the break is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a lâ€™un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 And then prepare the fracture with your hands, and if you find it fragmented, you must cut into it; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, strike it with one of the incisors you have; but place this tool under a forceps to avoid damage:
et semble une cuiller, et nâ€™est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de lâ€™os et la possance de lâ€™uevre; et ait II chiÃ©s, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez dâ€™aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and it resembles a spoon, and is not made of wood, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and let it have two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound when you pull out the bones; and when you are sure that there is no abscess, sew up the wound, and if the opening is small or you suspect an abscess, fill the wound with cloths and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	 And if there are abscesses there, then soak the cloth in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it on top.
Li estrignement de lâ€™os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus lâ€™os lâ€™enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et dâ€™aubun dâ€™uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz lâ€™assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende dâ€™une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et lâ€™emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et lâ€™envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met lâ€™estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz lâ€™asselle sainne, et desoz lâ€™asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus lâ€™os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz lâ€™assele, por lever lâ€™ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par lâ€™aligement de lâ€™espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens nâ€™i vient, juscâ€™a XX jors; puis rencomence lâ€™emplaustre, se tu vois quâ€™il en ait mestier, et lâ€™estraint et le laisse ensi, tant quâ€™il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And the setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without injury, is that you place on the bone an emplaster made from mill dust and the white of an egg, and put light wool on top, and under the arm if necessary; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then put the folded cloth over the wool and the emplaster; then take a fine strap three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and place the strap over the break, and turn the bandage up over the shoulder, and under the armpit, and under the injured arm; and secure each end, and when you see that the bandage holds the break properly, and you clearly see that the strap does not move over the broken bone, then loosen it daily, and when the ligature comes undone, then resecure it; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the arm to raise the shoulder up; this will lighten the break of the collarbone through the raising of the shoulder, where you bind the arm to the neck, and do not unbind it unless something bad happens, for twenty days; then renew the emplaster if necessary, and secure it and leave it thus until it is healed; and it is healed in twenty-eight days or less in some men.
de la brisure de lâ€™espaule	 Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si lâ€™apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun dâ€™uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de lâ€™espaule, et se desoz lâ€™estele est chevemens en aucun leu de lâ€™espaule, si emple celle cheveure dâ€™estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis lâ€™estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois kâ€™il amolist, si lâ€™estraint, et met igal lâ€™estele sâ€™elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce nâ€™est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It happens that the shoulder is fractured either in the large or middle part, and not from a fall; then prepare it according to the shape of the fracture, and set it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powdered flour with plenty of egg, and light stuffing, and put on double cloth; then put on a wide and thin board, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there are gaps under the board in any part of the shoulder, fill those gaps with linen stuffing, so that the board sits evenly; and then bind it all tightly with a large bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and look at the ligature every day; and every time it loosens, bind it again, and adjust the board if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is completed, unbind him, and be sure, for this is not a bone that can easily be displaced again.
Et se une piece de lâ€™os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et lâ€™oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele dâ€™apaisier aposteme chaut.	 And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and points beneath the heart, then slice it off, and do as we have said in the breakage of the rib to appease the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	 of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the toe.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute dâ€™alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en lâ€™os brisiÃ©s, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of breath, and thirst, and possibly vomits blood, and opens the crack in the broken bone, and one can see it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de lâ€™os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus lâ€™estele subtil de salz, ou dâ€™autre fust legier, et lâ€™envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus lâ€™os brisiet, si quâ€™elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et lâ€™estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et sâ€™elle ramolist, si lâ€™estraint; et sâ€™il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie lâ€™emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne lâ€™emplaustre, et lâ€™estraint tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And the treatment is such that the patient lies on his back, and one places a pillow between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and gathers the ribs from the second rib to the hands, and tries in all ways possible to make the bone as equal as possible; then place splints and bandages on top of the fine cloth of salt or other light wood, and wrap it in a thin cloth, and tie it tightly on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the cord smoothly around the back, and tighten it properly, and check every hour to see if the binding has loosened; and if it has loosened, then tighten it again; and if it needs to be untied due to swelling or itching that occurs in the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, and remove the splint, and proceed with the manner of cures; then retighten the splint, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	 Of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprÃ©s le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu quâ€™eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a lâ€™inquisition as dois.	 Know that rib fractures come only in large bones behind the back and inside the head, and they break only because they are brittle; and one feels it well upon examination of the two (ribs).
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the treatment is that you align the fracture as needed.
Et puis met lâ€™emplaustre, et lâ€™estraint dâ€™une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply a poultice and hold it in place with a bandage, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et câ€™est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 And if the rib fracture is inward-slanting, the patient feels very great pain and piercing, as if from pleurisy, because the bone punctures the flesh; and he lies almost motionless, and soon vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a sign of serious illness, and the ancients have paid it much attention.
Et si a de ces qui dient quâ€™il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	 And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to expel the fracture by force.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz nâ€™i viegne, sâ€™il nâ€™i est venus.	 We do not do this, lest hot abscesses come, if they were not already present.
Et sâ€™il i est venus, si le saine.	 And if they have come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun dâ€™ous câ€™on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et câ€™est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse nâ€™atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 And some say that one should place cupping glasses on the spot to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass may attract superfluous humors to the spot due to the weakness of the body's constitution.
Et dirent aucun dâ€™ous câ€™on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	 And some say that one should cover the spot with a cloth moistened in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the breath equal all around, then treat it according to the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor quâ€™il ne puet soffrir par lâ€™os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier lâ€™os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, sâ€™elle est grans, et le curez dâ€™emplaustres, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure due to the bone piercing the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut open on the site of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the lung; and then one must saw the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu quâ€™il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if such abscesses come, then place moistened cloths in rose oil on them, and place them on the site; and treat the site as one would an abscess, and let it lie softly on the bed where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	 of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient kâ€™il ploie; et ausi a lâ€™espinee dou dos.	 Sometimes there is a fracture of the bones of the neck, and it often happens that they bend; and so for the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir sâ€™il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins dâ€™une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take care to see if his hands are softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches quâ€™il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et sâ€™il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de lâ€™os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, sâ€™on i met cure.	 Know that he is mortal in many situations, and if he moves them and feels well when they are stretched and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts a cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a lâ€™espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir sâ€™il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on lâ€™a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it is healthy or not, take heed if the feet are weakened, and if there are accidents that occur in the hands, and on the back there is flatulence and evacuation without will; and when one has placed it on its belly, there is also evacuation without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is placed on its back, it cannot sit.
Saiches quâ€™il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is mortal; do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	 And if these accidents do not happen to him, then the matter is less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes sâ€™il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus lâ€™espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf dâ€™uef, tant quâ€™il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie dâ€™un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant kâ€™il soit sanez.	 And the treatment is that you check if there is hot swelling, then place on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk until it is calmed; then place one of the comforting and drying poultices, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on the part where he feels pain, until it is healed. iÄ™
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste lâ€™os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, sâ€™elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure dâ€™oignement enjanrant char, tant quâ€™il soit sanez; et se li chiÃ©s de lâ€™os est brisiez, ki est apelez li Â«chiÃ©s de la koweÂ», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a lâ€™autre main a ton pooir, puis met lâ€™emplaustre et lâ€™estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis lâ€™estraint, et sâ€™il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et lâ€™oste, et cure la plaie tant quâ€™elle soit sanee.	 And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cut above the crown; and remove the bone, then close the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then heal it with ointment of fat meat, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is fractured, which is called the "head of the cow," insert your little finger of your left hand, and make it equal to the other hand at your power, then apply the poultice and bandage on top, if you need them; then bind it, and if there is a fracture, cut above, and remove it, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de lâ€™os de la hainche	 of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et sâ€™il avient, si nâ€™avient fuer câ€™un poc dâ€™amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 It often happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it is, there is no more than a slight shortening at the head; and it splits lengthwise, and slants to the side of the foot, causing pain in the area, and sharpness, and swelling as with a break.

And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above, as far as to be on top of the break; and know what sort the break is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, then make it equal so that it has a natural shape.

And if an abscess occurs there, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed down, and then put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as needed, if there is no bad occurrence; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de lâ€™ajutoire	 of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de lâ€™espaule, et sâ€™il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc lâ€™une des II manieres: dont lâ€™une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 The shoulder is the part between the arm and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a piece of wood filled with medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiÃ©s II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant quâ€™il viegne a lâ€™aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres lâ€™estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 And you put two knots at the two ends, and hang them up, and let the patient sit on a seat; then you throw his broken arm onto the wood, until it reaches the armpit, and has in its middle a piece of wood, then hang some heavy thing or the assistant pulls down; then the healer puts the break even with both hands together, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	 And the other method is such that one lifts the patient onto his heel, and binds his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants: one to hold what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other to hold below all I the ligaments, and each extends to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is very strong, then one holds the ligament below the fracture, and one above the fracture, and each of the assistants extends to his part.

And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, then you must place one ligament halfway below the armpit, and another towards the side, below the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is on the side, then you must place a light ligament, without strain, until the fracture is level with the place and the side; then set the fracture equally, as it should be, and hold it, lest an abscess form there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne lâ€™estraindre mie juscâ€™a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis lâ€™estraint, et li maniere de lâ€™estraindre si est que tu mettes lâ€™emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus lâ€™ajutoire, et met ta main sus lâ€™espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus lâ€™ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu dâ€™esteles, sâ€™aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os nâ€™est muez.	 And if boils come there, do not bind them at all for VII days, and put a wet cloth in ashes and rose oil on it until the boils are soothed; then bind it, and the method of binding is that you place the poultice on the break, then gather the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put the bandage on, and bind over the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in the position of stars, if anything prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use dâ€™esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi dâ€™espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans quâ€™elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com jâ€™ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 And if you doubt that the bone has moved, use stars, and place on the break a star wider and stronger than the others, and let there be between each star two fingers of space, and let each star be so large that it passes over the break by three fingers on each side; then bind over the stars, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, more strongly and less spaced apart.

de la brisure du bras	 of the arm fracture
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui Â«foscileÂ», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "radius" and "ulna"; one is small, and that is the one that follows the wrist; and the other is large, and that is the one under the little finger; sometimes only the large radius breaks, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griÃ©s que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small radius is broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing; but when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and worse than when both are broken together.
Se câ€™est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is the small fibula that is broken alone, then it should be stretched gently and set evenly.

And if it is the large fibula, then it should be stretched more strongly; and extend it on the pillow, and take the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small toe lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the pillow in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no labor; then let one servant extend his arm to the part below his hand or at the ankle, and another servant on the other above.

And then remove the cerate, and apply the plaster of milled powder with abundant egg, then place the bandages, and let the bandage on the break be always stronger, and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have VI bandages on the arm in various positions: whether the break is in one of the bones or in two; and apply more pressure on the break than elsewhere, and always less by stretching, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprÃ©s aucuns jors.	 And treat the limb and the ligament afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre dâ€™aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence lâ€™estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si lâ€™adresce.	 And then begin the tightening again, and if the ligament is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar thing, treat it thus.

de la brisure de la main	 Of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et nâ€™i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that at the back of the hand and at the joints of the fingers, breaks are rare, and only occur in many cases as dislocations.

Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois. de la cuixe brisie	 Of the broken thigh

The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is evident when it turns forward or backward; and the restoration is done by tying one ligament above the break and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et câ€™est quant li brisure est emmi lâ€™os.	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches his ligament equally to his side; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.

And as you go higher on the break, tighten it less; then hold the two thread ends that you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie 2 splints above them; then come back down to the thread's end near the foot; and make sure it doesn't move from its place. de la ruelle dou genoil	 of the tendon of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the tendon of the knee there is little breakage, but it folds many times.

de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non Â«mustelzÂ», et li autres est apelez Â«foscileÂ»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that the leg has II bones; one of which is called by the right name "mustelz," and the other is called "foscile"; and there are all sorts of breaks as they happen to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the workings are entirely similar. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the small bone is broken, it twists forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, then there is great pain and it can be seen clearly; and it turns downward.

Then provide traction, and make it straight, and tie the splints equally; but nevertheless, if the break is ugly and there are several pieces, then the traction should be less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.

de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et nâ€™i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.
