de la brisure de lâ€™os dou poignil	 of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis lâ€™encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant quâ€™il vient a lâ€™entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's birth canal is broken, make her sit with legs spread apart, then lean her towards the back part, and hold her from behind; then fill the opening of the birth canal with cotton, and put in as much as I am tall; then let the woman get up, and lift the back little by little, and then the cotton will jump, until it comes to the entrance of the birth canal, and the bone will return with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or thereabouts: the fracture will be healed, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a reed to its opening, and blow up the whole bladder in the birth canal; then inflate the reed strongly inside it, until the bladder is swollen within: the bone will return with the bladder; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de lâ€™ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en lâ€™os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the man's wrist is broken, or that of the woman, then restore it as we have said concerning the hip bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and use to them, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For a fracture signifies in many instances the right way of restoration; consider this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge dâ€™oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the case of a fractured penis, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 Of a fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement sâ€™elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de lâ€™ajutoire ou semblant, quâ€™il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, that he be cauterized now, so that the cauteries which we have mentioned may testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu nâ€™as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus nâ€™i vient.	 And if the wound heals, then stop it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if no abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration juscâ€™a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et nâ€™i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if such abscesses form, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, so that the abscess may be healed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about evil accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone appears on the surface of the wound exposed, then it is necessary that you carefully place it in your hands with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne tâ€™est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire quâ€™il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu quâ€™il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, kâ€™il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if the extension is not ready to be set equal in your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight fingers in length, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary that the doctor have three or four, as many as he needs for each fracture cure; and let it be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the member during your work, and let it be pointed at the front, and thicker towards the middle, like this:
Et est apelez Â«palaincheÂ», por coi il covient que li chiÃ©s corbes soit mis sus lou chief de lâ€™os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant kâ€™il reviegne, et soit igalz lâ€™un encontre lâ€™autre.	 Et est apelez Â«palaincheÂ», por coi il covient que li chiÃ©s corbes
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre lâ€™os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de lâ€™os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone so that the instrument may have control over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener lâ€™os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope dâ€™un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en lâ€™os dâ€™aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then cut off a suitable instrument for this, either an incising or sawing one, with your power; then raise what remains in the bone of roughness and small scales.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprÃ©s, saiches quâ€™il nâ€™est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant quâ€™il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se câ€™est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, quâ€™il nâ€™i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit lâ€™os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If you have done so that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put any ointment or other thing on the wound where there is oil, lest it bring forth putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound not be constrained with the break; and many times have foolish doctors done this, and have brought upon the patient either death or corruption at times; and let the constraint be gentler and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens nâ€™i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si nâ€™i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu dâ€™esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that evil will come to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it should not be covered with bandages; but wrap around it, in place of bandages, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprÃ©s I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaÃ§on et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two that the swelling on the wound increases, then remove everything you have put on it all together, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment of theriac and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant quâ€™il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And the limb must be prepared in such a way that the swelling runs down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adÃ©s bowe, saiches kâ€™il i a petites pieces dâ€™os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot heal but repeatedly opens, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these displaced pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu quâ€™il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or another form of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is said in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de lâ€™ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant quâ€™il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprÃ©s XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not extract it, for many times this leads to death. But leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 Of the blows that come upon the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprÃ©s la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant câ€™est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see this after the health of the fracture, especially when it is close to the joint, and the appearance of the limb is unsightly; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun dâ€™uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et lâ€™estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est quâ€™il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de lâ€™oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant quâ€™ele soit ostee, et la cure tant quâ€™ele soit sanee.	 Take heed therefore if the wound is fresh: and administer styptic medicines to it, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, agaric, and similar others; and take one of these things or all together, and cook them with wine or with plenty of egg yolk or with honey; and place them on the wound in cloths, and bind it well, and do not untie it for many days; and then unbind it, and begin another, until the swelling is gone; or you may bandage it on a well-made piece of lead; for one of the properties of lead is that it removes all inflammations from the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then scrape off the surface, and make the superfluous part evident; or you may have it removed by a scraper, until it is gone, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprÃ©s la garison	 of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de lâ€™os est restoree, et demoure aprÃ©s li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi lâ€™une est por ceu quâ€™il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu quâ€™il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude dâ€™arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu quâ€™il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the break of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and delicate afterwards, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as needed; or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or because of excessive bleeding; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et lâ€™arose sovent dâ€™aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the treatment is that you have the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood is increased in him; and give baths to him, and bring him joy and happiness; then put wax on the limb, so that the wax attracts great nourishment to it, and wash it often with warm water, so that the nourishment reaches the limb; and let it regain its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprÃ©s la santeit	 of the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprÃ©s la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient câ€™on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient kâ€™il soient arosez dâ€™aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bones are visible, and the form of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb again completely; and many foolish doctors have done this in our land. And these works are blamed, and great evils come from them, and perhaps death. However, if the swelling and pain are fresh, it is necessary to apply hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of marsh mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, like well-made diaculum, and you take the marshmallow ointment, and mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top. Or you take fat figs, and grind them with coltsfoot powder, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continuously and vigorously rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let there be gentle movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de lâ€™oster au fer, si la covient coper juscâ€™a lâ€™os, a lâ€™incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the swelling is hardened like stone and needs to be removed with an iron instrument, it must be cut down to the bone with a fine incision; and apply caution and skill in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue dâ€™aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 A dislocation is a separation of any joint from its proper place, so that it cannot move; the limb is misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When a dislocation occurs in someone, they must be immediately brought back to their senses without delaying.
Car sâ€™on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie câ€™on le mueve a lâ€™oure kâ€™il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre dâ€™aigue chaude et dâ€™oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Car si on tarde, the place swells, and perhaps it can be reset with difficulty; therefore, it should not be moved when it is swollen: many times it brings spasm and other pains; however, when this happens, let the patient rest, then leave until the abscess is calmed; then rinse the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset, and treat each limb as it returns to its place.
Et jâ€™ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief juscâ€™a piez.	 And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations dâ€™ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche quâ€™il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 Rarely does it happen that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are slightly removed from their place and softened somewhat; or they are entirely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and saliva flows from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is entangled with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through many dispositions.
Et sâ€™elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de lâ€™une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide quâ€™il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it, and do not delay; and in such a way that the servant holds the patient's head, and the surgeon places his finger of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and let the other two fingers be ready, to make it even; and instruct the patient to soften their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant quâ€™elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the surgeon puts it back in place until it returns to its proper location.
Et se li ramener est griÃ©s, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose dâ€™aigue chaude et dâ€™oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the resetting is difficult, even if they are both jaws together, then soak them in hot water and oil until they can be easily reset; do not delay in setting them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait dâ€™oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiÃ©s soit estans entre II cussins, si quâ€™il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne sâ€™efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce quâ€™il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie dâ€™ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are brought back equally, and the patient's mouth is closed without softening, put on wet cloths in a plaster made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bands; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head stationary between two pillows, so that it does not move to the right or left, nor should they strive to speak, but take light food until the pains are removed, and the jaws are fixed; and then chew what they want lightly, and do not struggle to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well fixed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jaws cannot be set right within an hour and are not returned to their places, fever and customary seizures may ensue, and possibly stomach upset, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que câ€™est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, know that it is a sign of death; and many times the one to whom it happens dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the hand
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The fingers cannot dislocate from the side within the continuity of itself and from below, and sometimes they are dislocated backwards, and it is felt well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus lâ€™emplaustre et lou bendeil, et lâ€™estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus lâ€™emplaustre et le bendeil, et lâ€™estraint, et coumande au malaide quâ€™il se repose tant quâ€™il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiÃ©s de lâ€™espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back and extends his arms; then press strongly on the spot with your palm, and it will return to its place; then apply a poultice and bind it tightly; and the shoulder towards the elbow cannot dislocate; if not, and if it sometimes dislocates, reset it in its place, as we have said; then apply a poultice and bind it tightly, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus also is the shoulder blade restored when it has deviated from its place.
de la dislocation de lâ€™espaule	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule nâ€™est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi lâ€™une est quâ€™ele desalue a la partie de lâ€™assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por lâ€™espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers lâ€™assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates towards the lower part of the armpit; and the second is towards the upper arm; and occasionally dislocates towards the top, which happens rarely; and does not dislocate to the back due to the shoulder, nor to the inside due to the nerves. And often dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those with little flesh, because it jumps out quickly for them; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps out with difficulty and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule dâ€™un aposteme chaut, et cuide quâ€™elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And it happens to some men through a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu lâ€™esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary for you to test it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers lâ€™assele, et met difference entre lâ€™espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de lâ€™espaule une fosse, et desoz lâ€™assele au tochier le chief de lâ€™espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, sâ€™elle est desaluee en haut, si nâ€™est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation nâ€™est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it is down towards the shoulder blade, and it makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them manifest diversity; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the shoulder blade at the back of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the back; and this manner of dislocation is not hard to reset, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz lâ€™assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et lâ€™estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the attendant lifts the patient's hand up, then places his fingers beneath it, and forcibly raises the joint upward; and the attendant lifts the hand and extends it upward, then places it beneath; thus it will come quickly.
Et sâ€™elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprÃ©s, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz lâ€™assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de lâ€™espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si quâ€™il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute sâ€™espaule desoz lâ€™assele dou malaide, et lieve lâ€™assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en lâ€™ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said within several days afterward, the patient must be bathed in hot water; and let the attendant gently apply a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of althaea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let it be applied; then let the patient lie on his back, and place beneath the joint a swath of cloth, not too soft nor too hard; then let the doctor place his heel upon the swath, and forcibly lift the shoulder, and draw out the patient's hand; and another attendant shall hold the patient's head so that it does not move downward; immediately that shoulder will return, and if you see it thus, reset it according to this manner: and it is that you have a man present who is larger than the patient; and let him stand straight beside the patient's side, and place his shoulder beneath the patient's joint, and lift the joint upward so that the patient hangs in the air; and another attendant shall draw the patient's hand downward toward the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too restless, then have something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.

de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et sâ€™est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations nâ€™est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure. des dislocations de la hainche	 Of hip dislocations

When the dislocation is in the hip, you should have the patient lie on their healthy side, then place the strap at the root of the thigh, and the place that is under the buttock, then extend the strap upward towards the buttock, and towards the groin; then let another assistant take his arms, and embrace the thick part of the sick thigh, and stretch it with all your might: thus it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.

Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piÃ©s dou malaide ensamble dâ€™un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, and soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief dâ€™un fust, and soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre quâ€™il embraice le chief de la cuixe, and soit uns others ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, quâ€™il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, and si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, and estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, and sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, and puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; and ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, quâ€™il ne blece lou malaide, and puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, and li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.
Sâ€™elle revient, câ€™est boin.	 If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place him on the table and press it as we have said in the dislocation, and let the patient lie on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que jâ€™ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine dâ€™estre sus lâ€™angre malaide, puis presse a lâ€™autre main, et lâ€™estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly according to what I have said; and let the physician place his hand on the affected ankle, then press with the other hand, and extend downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient quâ€™il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met lâ€™emplaustre, et lâ€™estrain dâ€™un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met lâ€™emplaustre sus; et se tu vois quâ€™elles soient igalz, si lâ€™estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is behind, it is not necessary to extend the affected leg downwards or raise it off the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated backwards, as we have said about lying on both hips; and let him lie on his face, and let the ligament be extended as we have said before, and someone must press on the joint at the table; and it will be ready when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then bring the thighs together, and apply the plaster, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and if he rests for three days or four, then unbind him, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, then bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and let him walk gently until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	 Of the knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: câ€™est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	 The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide quâ€™il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et sâ€™ele ne sâ€™aert a sa cuixe, saiches quâ€™il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe sâ€™il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est quâ€™il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met lâ€™emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides dâ€™aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not touch his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all [types] is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and place his foot on top of yours; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your thighs, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he lightly bends his leg at his thigh; and apply the bandage, and cause the leg to adhere to the thigh, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then unbind; and the patient should not attempt to walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres nâ€™est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant quâ€™il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not at all, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	 of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	 The ankles are sometimes swollen and completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and protrudes forward towards the dislocated part; the reduction should be gentle, and one should extend it gently with their hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis lâ€™estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; sâ€™elle revient, câ€™est bien; se ce non, si rencomence lâ€™ovraige, car il revient; et sâ€™il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, quâ€™il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, kâ€™il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adÃ©s entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on lâ€™estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, it is necessary that you make the patient sit upright, and have two assistants hold the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards and push the foot up nicely; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, restart the work because it will return; and if it cannot return like this, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly fix a stick in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around, so that it does not harm the patient; then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another extend the foot with their hands or with one bandage tied above the ankle; then each assistant extends equally, and the stick should always be between the patient's thighs to keep the patient still when extending; then place the master equally on top of the dislocation with his hands, and another assistant holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met lâ€™emplastre et estoupes sus, et lâ€™estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si lâ€™estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et sâ€™il va devant cel termine, ce nâ€™est mie seurtez quâ€™il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is perfectly healed, place the bandage and dressing on top, bind it very tightly, tie the foot to the leg, and protect the nerves that are on the back of the ankle, so that the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding softens, bind again; then remove it on the third or fourth day, and allow the patient to walk after four days; and if he goes before this time, it is not safe that he may not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu lâ€™apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if there are abscesses present, it is necessary that you calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	 of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et câ€™est legiere chose.	 When the toes are dislocated, it is necessary to straighten them beautifully without difficulty, and this is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant quâ€™il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il nâ€™i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiÃ©s, puis lâ€™estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant quâ€™il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any node of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table straight and upright, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is equal and nothing appears there, place under the sole of the foot a table with two legs, then tighten it strongly and leave it for three days, then remove it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	 of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu nâ€™es saiges en lâ€™art et tu ne lâ€™as useit longement, et se tu nâ€™es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu nâ€™i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, dâ€™oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde dâ€™entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que jâ€™ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de tâ€™arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with the dislocation and you want to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and careful, not bold; and use at the beginning of calming things, hot poultices, and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, now reset the member to its place before the poultice arrives; and when the member is in place, administer calming things, hot poultices, and treat the wound as it should be done with desiccated onions; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken, remove them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear according to what I have said, for this is worth more according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your arm and body.
Amen	 Amen
